         <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Vojvodina_Hungarians" title="Alliance of Vojvodina Hungarians">

         )

      <p>
       <b>
        Vojvodina
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Serbian Cyrillic alphabet">
        Serbian Cyrillic
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="sr-Cyrl" xml:lang="sr-Cyrl">
        Војводина
       </span>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Autonomous Province of Vojvodina
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">
        Serbian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="sr" xml:lang="sr">
        Аутономна Покрајина Војводина
       </span>
       /
       <i>
        Autonomna Pokrajina Vojvodina
       </i>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian" title="Help:IPA/Serbo-Croatian">
         [ʋǒjʋodina]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small class="nowrap">
        (
        <span class="unicode haudio">
         <span class="fn">
          <span style="white-space:nowrap">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Sr-Vd.ogg" title="About this sound">
            <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Sr-Vd.ogg" title="Sr-Vd.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       ; see
       <a href="#Name">
        Names in other languages
       </a>
       ), is an
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_administrative_division" title="Autonomous administrative division">
        autonomous province
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
        Serbia
       </a>
       , located in the northern part of the country, in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" title="Pannonian Plain">
        Pannonian Plain
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">
        Novi Sad
       </a>
       is the largest city and administrative center of Vojvodina and the second-largest city in Serbia. Vojvodina has a population of almost 2 million (nearly 27% of Serbia's population excluding
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">
        Kosovo
       </a>
       ). It has a multi-ethnic and
       <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">
        multi-cultural
       </a>
       identity;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       there are some 26
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">
        ethnic groups
       </a>
       in the province,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and six languages are in official use by the provincial administration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Name">
        Name
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The term
       <i>
        vojvodina
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">
        Serbian
       </a>
       means a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy" title="Duchy">
        duchy
       </a>
       – more specifically, a
       <a href="/wiki/Voivodeship" title="Voivodeship">
        voivodeship
       </a>
       . It derives from the word
       <i>
        "vojvoda"
       </i>
       (See:
       <a href="/wiki/Voivode" title="Voivode">
        voivode
       </a>
       ) which stems from the
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Slavic" title="Proto-Slavic">
        Proto-Slavic language
       </a>
       word
       <i>
        "voevoda"
       </i>
       . Those words are etymologically connected with modern-day words
       <i>
        "vojnik"
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Soldier" title="Soldier">
        soldier
       </a>
       ) and
       <i>
        "voditi"
       </i>
       (to lead). Its original name (from 1848) was the "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Voivodeship" title="Serbian Voivodeship">
        Serbian Voivodeship
       </a>
       " (Српска Војводина /
       <i>
        Srpska Vojvodina
       </i>
       ) which then became "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voivodeship_of_Serbia_and_Temes_Banat" title="Voivodeship of Serbia and Temes Banat">
        Voivodeship of Serbia
       </a>
       " (Војводство Србија /
       <i>
        Vojvodstvo Srbija
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The full official names of the province in all official languages of Vojvodina are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Serbian_language" title="Serbian language">
         Serbian
        </a>
        : Аутономна Покрајина Војводина /
        <i>
         Autonomna Pokrajina Vojvodina
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">
         Hungarian
        </a>
        :
        <i>
         Vajdaság Autonóm Tartomány
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">
         Slovak
        </a>
        :
        <i>
         Autonómna pokrajina Vojvodina
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">
         Romanian
        </a>
        :
        <i>
         Provincia Autonomă Voivodina
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">
         Croatian
        </a>
        :
        <i>
         Autonomna Pokrajina Vojvodina
        </i>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Rusyn_language" title="Pannonian Rusyn language">
         Pannonian Rusyn
        </a>
        : Автономна Покраїна Войводина (
        <i>
         Avtonomna Pokrajina Vojvodina
        </i>
        )
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Vojvodina" title="History of Vojvodina">
        History of Vojvodina
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           may be
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Section#Section_size_policies" title="Help:Section">
            too long
           </a>
           and excessively detailed.
          </b>
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please consider summarizing the material while
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CITE" title="Wikipedia:CITE">
            citing sources
           </a>
           as needed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (February 2012)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Roman_times_and_Roman_rule">
        Pre-Roman times and Roman rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-Roman times and Roman rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the Neolithic period, two important archaeological cultures flourished in this area: the
       <a href="/wiki/Star%C4%8Devo_culture" title="Starčevo culture">
        Starčevo culture
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Vin%C4%8Da_culture" title="Vinča culture">
        Vinča culture
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">
        Indo-European
       </a>
       peoples first settled in the territory of present-day Vojvodina in 3200 BC. During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eneolithic" title="Eneolithic">
        Eneolithic
       </a>
       period, the
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">
        Bronze Age
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">
        Iron Age
       </a>
       , several Indo-European archaeological cultures were centered in or around Vojvodina: the
       <a href="/wiki/Vu%C4%8Dedol_culture" title="Vučedol culture">
        Vučedol culture
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vinkovci_culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vinkovci culture (page does not exist)">
        Vinkovci culture
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Vatin_culture" title="Vatin culture">
        Vatin culture
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Belegi%C5%A1_culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Belegiš culture (page does not exist)">
        Belegiš culture
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Bosut_culture" title="Bosut culture">
        Bosut culture
       </a>
       , etc. Before the Roman conquest in the 1st century BC, Indo-European peoples of
       <a href="/wiki/Illyrians" title="Illyrians">
        Illyrian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thracian" title="Thracian">
        Thracian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">
        Celtic
       </a>
       origin inhabited this area. The first states organized in this area were the Celtic
       <a href="/wiki/Scordisci" title="Scordisci">
        State of the Scordisci
       </a>
       (3rd century BC-1st century AD) with capital in
       <a href="/wiki/Singidunum" title="Singidunum">
        Singidunum
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">
        Belgrade
       </a>
       ), and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dacian_Kingdom" title="Dacian Kingdom">
        Dacian Kingdom
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Burebista" title="Burebista">
        Burebista
       </a>
       (1st century BC).
      </p>
      <p>
       During Roman rule,
       <a href="/wiki/Sirmium" title="Sirmium">
        Sirmium
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Mitrovica" title="Sremska Mitrovica">
        Sremska Mitrovica
       </a>
       ) was one of the four capital cities of the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       , and six
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Emperors" title="Roman Emperors">
        Roman Emperors
       </a>
       were born in this city or in its surroundings. The city was also the capital of several Roman administrative units, including
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonia_Inferior" title="Pannonia Inferior">
        Pannonia Inferior
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonia_Secunda" title="Pannonia Secunda">
        Pannonia Secunda
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Pannonia" title="Diocese of Pannonia">
        Diocese of Pannonia
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Praetorian_prefecture_of_Illyricum" title="Praetorian prefecture of Illyricum">
        Praetorian prefecture of Illyricum
       </a>
       . Roman rule lasted until the 5th century, after which the region came into the possession of various peoples and states. While
       <a href="/wiki/Banat" title="Banat">
        Banat
       </a>
       was a part of the Roman province of
       <a href="/wiki/Dacia" title="Dacia">
        Dacia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Syrmia" title="Syrmia">
        Syrmia
       </a>
       belonged to the Roman province of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pannonia_(Roman_province)" title="Pannonia (Roman province)">
        Pannonia
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">
        Bačka
       </a>
       was not part of the Roman Empire and was populated and ruled by Sarmatian
       <a href="/wiki/Iazyges" title="Iazyges">
        Iazyges
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Middle_Ages_and_Slavic_settlement">
        Early Middle Ages and Slavic settlement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early Middle Ages and Slavic settlement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       After the Romans were driven away from this region, various Indo-European and Turkic peoples and states ruled in the area. These peoples included Goths, Sarmatians, Huns, Gepids and Avars. For regional history, the largest in importance was a Gepid state, which had its capital in Sirmium. According to the 7th-century
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Miracles_of_Saint_Demetrius" title="Miracles of Saint Demetrius">
         Miracles of Saint Demetrius
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">
        Avars
       </a>
       gave the region of Syrmia to a Bulgar leader named
       <a href="/wiki/Kuber" title="Kuber">
        Kuber
       </a>
       circa 680. The Bulgars of Kuber moved south with Maurus to Macedonia where they co-operated with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tervel" title="Tervel">
        Tervel
       </a>
       in the 8th century.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2362" data-file-width="3726" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg/220px-Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg/330px-Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg/440px-Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ara%C4%8Da_5.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ruins of
         <a href="/wiki/Ara%C4%8Da" title="Arača">
          Arača
         </a>
         church
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">
        Slavs
       </a>
       settled today's Vojvodina in the 6th and 7th centuries,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       before some of them crossed the rivers Sava and Danube and settled in the Balkans. Slavic tribes that lived in the territory of present-day Vojvodina included Abodrites, Severans, Braničevci and Timočani. In the 9th century, after the fall of the Avar state, the first forms of Slavic statehood emerged in this area. The first Slavic states that ruled over this region included the Bulgarian Empire,
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">
        Great Moravia
       </a>
       and Ljudevit's Pannonian Duchy. During the Bulgarian administration (9th century), local Bulgarian dukes,
       <a href="/wiki/Salan" title="Salan">
        Salan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Glad_(duke)" title="Glad (duke)">
        Glad
       </a>
       , ruled over the region. Salan's residence was Titel, while that of Glad was possibly in the rumoured rampart of Galad or perhaps in the Kladovo (Gladovo) in eastern Serbia. Glad's descendant was the duke Ahtum, another local ruler from the 11th century who opposed the establishment of Hungarian rule over the region.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the village of
       <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Celarevo" title="Čelarevo">
        Čelarevo
       </a>
       archaeologists have also found traces of people who practised the Judaic religion. Bunardžić dated Avar-Bulgar graves excavated in Čelarevo, containing skulls with Mongolian features and Judaic symbols, to the late 8th and 9th centuries. Erdely and Vilkhnovich consider the graves to belong to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kabars" title="Kabars">
        Kabars
       </a>
       who eventually broke ties with the Khazar Empire between the 830s and 862. (Three other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khazar" title="Khazar">
        Khazar
       </a>
       tribes joined the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magyars" title="Magyars">
        Magyars
       </a>
       and took part in the Magyar conquest of the Carpathian basin including what is now Vojvodina in 895-907.)
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hungarian_rule">
        Hungarian rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hungarian rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7,%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90,%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..,,.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2711" data-file-width="2643" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7%2C%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90%2C%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..%2C%2C.jpg/220px-%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7%2C%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90%2C%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..%2C%2C.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7%2C%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90%2C%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..%2C%2C.jpg/330px-%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7%2C%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90%2C%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..%2C%2C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7%2C%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90%2C%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..%2C%2C.jpg/440px-%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7%2C%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90%2C%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..%2C%2C.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D0%90%D0%A7,%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%88%D0%92%D0%9E%D0%94%D0%98%D0%9D%D0%90,%D0%A1%D0%A0%D0%91%D0%98%D0%88%D0%90..,,.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8D_Fortress" title="Bač Fortress">
          Bač Fortress
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following territorial disputes with Byzantine and Bulgarian states, most of Vojvodina became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       between 10th and 12th century and remained under Hungarian administration until the 16th century (Following periods of Ottoman and Habsburg administrations, Hungarian political dominance over most of the region was established again in 1867 and over entire region in 1882, after abolition of the Habsburg Military Frontier).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The regional demographic balance started changing in the 11th century when Magyars began to replace the local Slavic population. But from the 14th century, the balance changed again in favour of the Slavs when Serbian refugees fleeing from territories conquered by the Ottoman army settled in the area. Most
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hungarian_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hungarian-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of the Hungarians left the region during Ottoman conquest and early period of Ottoman administration, so the population of Vojvodina in Ottoman times was predominantly Serbs (who comprised an absolute majority of Vojvodina at the time
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hungarian_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-hungarian-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) and Muslims.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hungarian_7-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-hungarian-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_rule">
        Ottoman rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ottoman rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       After the defeat of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Kingdom of Hungary in the Middle Ages">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Moh%C3%A1cs" title="Mohács">
        Mohács
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       , the region fell into a period of anarchy and civil wars. In 1526
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emperor_Jovan_Nenad" title="Emperor Jovan Nenad">
        Jovan Nenad
       </a>
       , a leader of Serb mercenaries, established his rule in
       <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">
        Bačka
       </a>
       , northern
       <a href="/wiki/Banat" title="Banat">
        Banat
       </a>
       and a small part of
       <a href="/wiki/Syrmia" title="Syrmia">
        Syrmia
       </a>
       . He created an ephemeral independent state, with
       <a href="/wiki/Subotica" title="Subotica">
        Subotica
       </a>
       as its capital. At the peak of his power, Jovan Nenad proclaimed himself Serbian Emperor in Subotica. Taking advantage of the extremely confused military and political situation, the Hungarian noblemen from the region joined forces against him and defeated the Serbian troops in the summer of 1527. Emperor Jovan Nenad was assassinated and his state collapsed. After the fall of emperor's state, the supreme military commander of Jovan Nenad's army,
       <a href="/wiki/Radoslav_%C4%8Celnik" title="Radoslav Čelnik">
        Radoslav Čelnik
       </a>
       , established his own temporary state in the region of Syrmia, where he ruled as Ottoman vassal.
      </p>
      <p>
       A few decades later, the whole region was added to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       , which ruled over it until the end of the 17th and the first half of the 18th century, when it was incorporated into the
       <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">
        Habsburg Monarchy
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Karlowitz" title="Treaty of Karlowitz">
        Treaty of Karlowitz
       </a>
       of 1699, between
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">
        Holy League
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       , marked the withdrawal of the Ottoman forces from
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central Europe
       </a>
       , and the supremacy of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" title="Habsburg Empire">
        Habsburg Empire
       </a>
       in that part of the continent. According to the treaty, western part of Vojvodina passed to Habsburgs. Eastern part of it (eastern Syrmia and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teme%C5%9Fvar_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" title="Temeşvar Province, Ottoman Empire">
        Province of Tamışvar
       </a>
       ) remained in Ottoman hands until Austrian conquest in 1716. This new border change is ratified by the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Passarowitz" title="Treaty of Passarowitz">
        Treaty of Passarowitz
       </a>
       in 1718.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Habsburg_rule">
        Habsburg rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Habsburg rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="437" data-file-width="600" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg/220px-Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg/330px-Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg/440px-Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blagovestenski_sabor_1861.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Blagoveštenski assembly in Sremski Karlovci, 1861
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Serb_Migrations" title="Great Serb Migrations">
        Great Serb Migration
       </a>
       , Serbs from Ottoman territories settled in the Habsburg Monarchy at the end of the 17th century (in 1690), most of whom settled what is now Hungary, the lesser part settling in western Vojvodina. However, because of this event, all Serbs in the Habsburg Monarchy gained the status of a recognized nation with extensive rights, in exchange for providing a border militia (in the
       <a href="/wiki/Military_Frontier" title="Military Frontier">
        Military Frontier
       </a>
       ) that could be mobilized against invaders from the south, as well as in case of civil unrest in the Habsburg Kingdom of Hungary.
      </p>
      <p>
       At the beginning of Habsburg rule, most of the region was integrated into the Military Frontier, while western parts of Bačka were put under civil administration within the County of Bač. Later, the civil administration was expanded to other (mostly northern) parts of the region, while southern parts remained under military administration. The eastern part of it was held by the Ottomans between 1787–1788, during the
       <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1787%E2%80%931792)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1787–1792)">
        Russo-Turkish War
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1716,
       <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">
        Vienna
       </a>
       temporarily forbade settlement by Hungarians and
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       in the area, while large numbers of German speakers were settled in the region. From 1782,
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestant
       </a>
       Hungarians and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_Germans" title="Ethnic Germans">
        ethnic Germans
       </a>
       settled in larger numbers.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="924" data-file-width="717" height="284" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png/220px-Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png/330px-Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png/440px-Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Serbia_and_Vojvodina_1848.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Proclaimed borders of Serbian Vojvodina at the May Assembly (1848) and autonomous Ottoman
         <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">
          Principality of Serbia
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the 1848-49 revolutions, Vojvodina was a site of war between Serbs and Hungarians, due to the opposite national conceptions of these two peoples. At the
       <a href="/wiki/May_Assembly" title="May Assembly">
        May Assembly
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Sremski_Karlovci" title="Sremski Karlovci">
        Sremski Karlovci
       </a>
       (13–15 May 1848),
       <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">
        Serbs
       </a>
       declared the constitution of the
       <b>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_Voivodship" title="Serbian Voivodship">
         Serbian Voivodship
        </a>
       </b>
       (Serbian Duchy), a Serbian autonomous region within the
       <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">
        Austrian Empire
       </a>
       . The Serbian Voivodship consisted of Srem, Bačka, Banat, and
       <a href="/wiki/Baranya_(region)" title="Baranya (region)">
        Baranja
       </a>
       . The head of the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitanate_of_Karlovci" title="Metropolitanate of Karlovci">
        metropolitanate of Sremski Karlovci
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Josif_Raja%C4%8Di%C4%87" title="Josif Rajačić">
        Josif Rajačić
       </a>
       , was elected
       <a href="/wiki/Patriarchate_of_Karlovci" title="Patriarchate of Karlovci">
        patriarch
       </a>
       , while
       <a href="/wiki/Stevan_%C5%A0upljikac" title="Stevan Šupljikac">
        Stevan Šupljikac
       </a>
       was chosen as first
       <a href="/wiki/Voivode" title="Voivode">
        voivod
       </a>
       (duke). The ethnic war hit this area perhaps the hardest, with terrible atrocities committed against the civilian populations by both sides.
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the Habsburg and Serb victory over the Hungarians in 1849, a new administrative territory was created in the region in November 1849, in accordance with a decision made by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian_emperor" title="Austrian emperor">
        Austrian emperor
       </a>
       . By this decision, the Serbian autonomous region created in 1848 was transformed into the new Austrian
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_land" title="Crown land">
        crown land
       </a>
       known as
       <b>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voivodeship_of_Serbia_and_Temes_Banat" title="Voivodeship of Serbia and Temes Banat">
         Voivodeship of Serbia and Temes Banat
        </a>
       </b>
       . It consisted of Banat, Bačka and Srem, excluding the southern parts of these regions which were part of the Military Frontier. An Austrian governor seated in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timi%C5%9Foara" title="Timişoara">
        Temeschwar
       </a>
       ruled the area, while the title of Voivod belonged to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian_Emperor" title="Austrian Emperor">
        emperor
       </a>
       himself. The full title of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrian_Emperor" title="Austrian Emperor">
        emperor
       </a>
       was "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grosswojwod" title="Grosswojwod">
        Grand Voivod
       </a>
       of the Voivodship of Serbia" (German:
       <i>
        Großwoiwode der Woiwodschaft Serbien
       </i>
       ). German and Illyrian (Serbian) were the official languages of the crown land. In 1860, the new province was abolished and most of it (with exception of Syrmia) was again integrated into the Habsburg
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       . After 1867, the Kingdom of Hungary became one of two self-governing parts of
       <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">
        Austria-Hungary
       </a>
       . The era following the
       <a href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Compromise_of_1867" title="Austro-Hungarian Compromise of 1867">
        Austro-Hungarian Compromise of 1867
       </a>
       was a period of economic flourishing, since Kingdom of Hungary had the second fastest growing economy in Europe between 1867–1913, but ethnic relations were strained. According to the 1910 census, the last census conducted in Austria-Hungary, the population of Vojvodina included 510,754 (33.8%) Serbs, 425,672 (28.1%) Hungarians and 324,017 (21.4%) Germans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia.2C_World_War_II.2C_socialist_Yugoslavia">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia,_World_War_II,_socialist_Yugoslavia">
        Kingdom of Yugoslavia, World War II, socialist Yugoslavia
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Yugoslavia, World War II, socialist Yugoslavia">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (September 2016)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="328" data-file-width="975" height="74" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg/220px-Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg/330px-Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg/440px-Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Novog_Sada.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">
          Novi Sad
         </a>
         , at the beginning of 20th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       At the end of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       , the Austro-Hungarian Empire collapsed. On 29 October 1918, Syrmia became a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/State_of_Slovenes,_Croats_and_Serbs" title="State of Slovenes, Croats and Serbs">
        State of Slovenes, Croats and Serbs
       </a>
       . On 31 October 1918, the
       <a href="/wiki/Banat_Republic" title="Banat Republic">
        Banat Republic
       </a>
       was proclaimed in
       <a href="/wiki/Timi%C8%99oara" title="Timișoara">
        Timișoara
       </a>
       . The government of Hungary recognized its independence, but it was short-lived.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 25 November 1918, the Assembly of Serbs, Bunjevci, and other nations of Vojvodina in Novi Sad proclaimed the unification of Vojvodina (
       <a href="/wiki/Banat,_Ba%C4%8Dka_and_Baranja" title="Banat, Bačka and Baranja">
        Banat, Bačka and Baranja
       </a>
       ) with the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">
        Kingdom of Serbia
       </a>
       (The assembly numbered 757 deputies, of which 578 were
       <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">
        Serbs
       </a>
       , 84
       <a href="/wiki/Bunjevci" title="Bunjevci">
        Bunjevci
       </a>
       , 62
       <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">
        Slovaks
       </a>
       , 21
       <a href="/wiki/Rusyns" title="Rusyns">
        Rusyn
       </a>
       , 6
       <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">
        Germans
       </a>
       , 3
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0okci" title="Šokci">
        Šokci
       </a>
       , 2
       <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">
        Croats
       </a>
       and 1
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magyars" title="Magyars">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       ). One day before this, on 24 November, the Assembly of Syrmia also proclaimed the unification of Syrmia with Serbia. On 1 December 1918, Vojvodina (as part of the Kingdom of Serbia) officially became part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbs,_Croats_and_Slovenes" title="Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes">
        Kingdom of Serbs, Croats and Slovenes
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1101" data-file-width="2006" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg/220px-Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg/330px-Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg/440px-Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Velika-narodna-skupstina-1918.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Assembly of Serbs, Bunjevci, and other nations of Vojvodina in Novi Sad proclaimed the unification of Vojvodina region with the Kingdom of Serbia, 1918.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Between 1929 and 1941, the region became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube_Banovina" title="Danube Banovina">
        Danube Banovina
       </a>
       , a province of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">
        Kingdom of Yugoslavia
       </a>
       . Its capital city was Novi Sad. Apart from the core territories of Vojvodina and Baranja, it included significant parts of
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0umadija" title="Šumadija">
        Šumadija
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Brani%C4%8Devo_(region)" title="Braničevo (region)">
        Braničevo
       </a>
       regions south of the Danube (but not the
       <a href="/wiki/Belgrade_City_Administration_(1929%E2%80%9341)" title="Belgrade City Administration (1929–41)">
        capital city of Belgrade
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 1941 and 1944, during
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" title="Axis Powers">
        Axis Powers
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       and its allies,
       <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">
        Independent State of Croatia
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungary_during_World_War_II" title="Hungary during World War II">
        Hungary
       </a>
       ) divided and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Vojvodina,_1941-1944" title="Occupation of Vojvodina, 1941-1944">
        occupied Vojvodina
       </a>
       . Bačka and Baranja were annexed by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horthy" title="Horthy">
        Horthy
       </a>
       's Hungary and Syrmia was included into the
       <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">
        Independent State of Croatia
       </a>
       . A smaller Danube Banovina (including Banat, Šumadija, and Braničevo) existed as part of the area governed by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_Administration_in_Serbia" title="Military Administration in Serbia">
        Military Administration in Serbia
       </a>
       . The administrative center of this smaller province was
       <a href="/wiki/Smederevo" title="Smederevo">
        Smederevo
       </a>
       . However, Banat itself was a separate autonomous region ruled by its German minority. The occupying powers committed numerous crimes against the civilian population, especially against Serbs, Jews and Roma; the Jewish population of Vojvodina was almost completely killed or deported. In total, Axis (German, Croatian and Hungarian) occupational authorities killed about 50,000 citizens of Vojvodina (mostly Serbs, Jews and Roma) while more than 280,000 people were interned, arrested, violated or tortured.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Axis occupation ended in 1944 and the region was temporarily placed under military administration (1944–1945) run by the new communist authorities. During and after the military administration, several thousands of citizens were killed - this affected mostly ethnic Germans, but also one part of Hungarian and Serb populations. Both the war-time Axis occupational authorities and the post-war communist authorities ran concentration/prison camps in the territory of Vojvodina. (see
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_concentration_and_internment_camps" title="List of concentration and internment camps">
        List of concentration and internment camps
       </a>
       ). While war-time prisoners in these camps were mostly Jews, Serbs and communists, post-war camps were formed for ethnic Germans (
       <a href="/wiki/Danube_Swabians" title="Danube Swabians">
        Danube Swabians
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Most Vojvodina Germans (about 200,000) fled the region in 1944, together with the defeated German army.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of those who remained in the region (about 150,000) were sent to some of the villages cordoned off as prisons. It is estimated that some 48,447 Germans died in the camps from disease, hunger, malnutrition, mistreatment, and cold. Some 8,049 Germans were killed by partisans during military administration in Vojvodina after October 1944.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has also been estimated that post-war communist authorities killed some 15,000-20,000
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hungarians and some 23,000-24,000
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mail-archive1_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mail-archive1-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Serbs during
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_purges_in_Serbia_in_1944%E2%80%9345" title="Communist purges in Serbia in 1944–45">
        Communist purges in Serbia in 1944–45
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       According to Professor Dragoljub Živković,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (January 2017)">
           who?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       47,000 ethnic Serbs were killed in Vojvodina during entire 1941-1948 period. About half of that number were killed by occupational forces and another half were killed by post-war communist authorities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mail-archive1_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mail-archive1-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The region was politically restored in 1944 (incorporating Syrmia, Banat, Bačka, and Baranja) and became an autonomous province of Serbia in 1945. Instead of the previous name (Danube Banovina), the region regained its historical name of Vojvodina, while its capital city remained Novi Sad. When final borders of Vojvodina were defined, Baranja was assigned to Croatia, while northern part of Mačva region was assigned to Vojvodina. At first, the province enjoyed only a small level of autonomy within Serbia, but it gained extensive rights of self-rule under the 1974 Yugoslav constitution, which gave both Kosovo and Vojvodina
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       veto power in the Serbian and Yugoslav parliaments, as changes to their status could not be made without the consent of the two Provincial Assemblies. The 1974 Serbian constitution, adopted at the same time, reiterated that "the Socialist Republic of Serbia comprises the
       <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Vojvodina" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Vojvodina">
        Socialist Autonomous Province of Vojvodina
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo" title="Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo">
        Socialist Autonomous Province of Kosovo
       </a>
       , which originated in the common struggle of nations and nationalities of Yugoslavia in the National Liberation War (the Second World War) and socialist revolution".
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Under the rule of the later Serbian president
       <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">
        Slobodan Milošević
       </a>
       and after a series of protests against Vojvodina's party leadership during the summer and autumn of 1988, which forced it to resign and eventually accept Serbia's constitutional amendments that practically dismissed the autonomy of the provinces in Serbia, Vojvodina and Kosovo finally lost elements of statehood in September 1990 when the new constitution of the Republic of Serbia was adopted. Vojvodina was still referred to as an autonomous province of Serbia, but most of its autonomous powers – including, crucially, its vote on the Yugoslav collective presidency – were transferred to the control of Belgrade. The province, however, still had its own parliament and government and some other autonomous functions as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_period">
        Contemporary period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Contemporary period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">

           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

           </a>
          </b>

          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit">

           </a>

           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">

           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (December 2016)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">

            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">

           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The fall of Milošević in 2000 created a new political climate in Vojvodina. Following talks between the political parties, the level of the province's
       <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/autonomy" title="wikt:autonomy">
        autonomy
       </a>
       was somewhat increased by the
       <a href="/wiki/Omnibus_law" title="Omnibus law">
        omnibus law
       </a>
       in 2002. The Vojvodina provincial assembly adopted a new statute on 15 October 2008, which, partly amended, was approved by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Serbia" title="Parliament of Serbia">
        Parliament of Serbia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg/170px-%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg/255px-%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg/340px-%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A1%D0%B0_%D0%9E%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B3_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D1%98%D0%B8%D1%88%D1%82%D0%B0.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">
          National park
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">
          Fruška Gora
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B,_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3072" data-file-width="4608" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B%2C_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B%2C_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B%2C_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B%2C_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B%2C_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B%2C_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%9A%D0%98%D0%A6_%D0%9F%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%9B,_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%99_14.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pali%C4%87_lake" title="Palić lake">
          Palić lake
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Vojvodina is situated in the northern quarter of
       <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
        Serbia
       </a>
       , in the southeast part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" title="Pannonian Plain">
        Pannonian Plain
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">
        plain
       </a>
       that remained when the
       <a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">
        Pliocene
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Sea" title="Pannonian Sea">
         Pannonian Sea
        </a>
       </i>
       dried out. As a consequence of this, Vojvodina is rich in fertile
       <a href="/wiki/Loam" title="Loam">
        loamy
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Loess" title="Loess">
        loess
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Soil" title="Soil">
        soil
       </a>
       , covered with a layer of
       <a href="/wiki/Chernozem" title="Chernozem">
        chernozem
       </a>
       . The region is divided by the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tisza" title="Tisza">
        Tisa
       </a>
       rivers into:
       <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%8Dka" title="Bačka">
        Bačka
       </a>
       in the northwest,
       <a href="/wiki/Banat" title="Banat">
        Banat
       </a>
       in the east and
       <a href="/wiki/Syrmia" title="Syrmia">
        Syrmia
       </a>
       (Srem) in the southwest. A small part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ma%C4%8Dva" title="Mačva">
        Mačva
       </a>
       region is also located in Vojvodina, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Srem_District" title="Srem District">
        Srem District
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Today, the western part of
       <a href="/wiki/Syrmia" title="Syrmia">
        Syrmia
       </a>
       is in
       <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
        Croatia
       </a>
       , the northern part of Bačka is in
       <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">
        Hungary
       </a>
       , the eastern part of Banat is in
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       (with a small piece in Hungary), while
       <a href="/wiki/Baranya_(region)" title="Baranya (region)">
        Baranja
       </a>
       (which is between the Danube and the
       <a href="/wiki/Drava" title="Drava">
        Drava
       </a>
       ) is in Hungary and Croatia. Vojvodina has a total surface area of 21,500 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (8,300 sq mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Vojvodina is also part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danube-Kris-Mures-Tisza" title="Danube-Kris-Mures-Tisza">
        Danube-Kris-Mures-Tisa
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Euroregion" title="Euroregion">
        euroregion
       </a>
       . The Gudurica peak (Gudurički vrh) on the
       <a href="/wiki/Vr%C5%A1ac_Mountains" title="Vršac Mountains">
        Vršac Mountains
       </a>
       , is the highest peak in Vojvodina, at an altitude of 641 m above sea level.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novi_Sad,_Mihajla_Pupina,_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3178" data-file-width="4770" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Novi_Sad%2C_Mihajla_Pupina%2C_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg/220px-Novi_Sad%2C_Mihajla_Pupina%2C_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Novi_Sad%2C_Mihajla_Pupina%2C_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg/330px-Novi_Sad%2C_Mihajla_Pupina%2C_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Novi_Sad%2C_Mihajla_Pupina%2C_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg/440px-Novi_Sad%2C_Mihajla_Pupina%2C_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novi_Sad,_Mihajla_Pupina,_budova_vl%C3%A1dy_Vojvodiny_ve%C4%8Der.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Banovina Palace, the seat of the Provincial
         <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Vojvodina" title="Government of Vojvodina">
          Government of Vojvodina
         </a>
         , at night
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Vojvodina" title="Politics of Vojvodina">
        Politics of Vojvodina
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vojvodina_provincial_elections,_2016" title="Vojvodina provincial elections, 2016">
        Vojvodina provincial elections, 2016
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_Vojvodina" title="Assembly of Vojvodina">
        Assembly of Vojvodina
       </a>
       is the provincial
       <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">
        legislature
       </a>
       composed of 120 proportionally elected members. The current members were elected in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vojvodina_provincial_elections,_2016" title="Vojvodina provincial elections, 2016">
        2016 provincial elections
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Vojvodina" title="Government of Vojvodina">
        Government of Vojvodina
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">
        executive
       </a>
       administrative body composed of a
       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Government_of_Vojvodina" title="President of the Government of Vojvodina">
        president
       </a>
       and cabinet ministers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The current ruling coalition in the Vojvodina parliament is composed of the following political parties:
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Progressive_Party" title="Serbian Progressive Party">
        Serbian Progressive Party
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Serbia" title="Socialist Party of Serbia">
        Socialist Party of Serbia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Vojvodina_Hungarians" title="Alliance of Vojvodina Hungarians">
        Alliance of Vojvodina Hungarians
       </a>
       . The current president of Vojvodinian government is
       <a href="/wiki/Igor_Mirovi%C4%87" title="Igor Mirović">
        Igor Mirović
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Progressive_Party" title="Serbian Progressive Party">
        Serbian Progressive Party
       </a>
       ), while the president of the provincial Assembly is
       <a href="/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_P%C3%A1sztor_(politician)" title="István Pásztor (politician)">
        István Pásztor
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Alliance_of_Vojvodina_Hungarians" title="Alliance of Vojvodina Hungarians">
        Alliance of Vojvodina Hungarians
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Vojvodina is divided into seven
       <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Serbia" title="Districts of Serbia">
        districts
       </a>
       . They are regional centers of state authority, but have no powers of their own; they present purely administrative divisions. The seven districts are further subdivided into 37
       <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_and_cities_of_Serbia" title="Municipalities and cities of Serbia">
        municipalities
       </a>
       and the 8 cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Kikinda" title="Kikinda">
        Kikinda
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad" title="Novi Sad">
        Novi Sad
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Subotica" title="Subotica">
        Subotica
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zrenjanin" title="Zrenjanin">
        Zrenjanin
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pan%C4%8Devo" title="Pančevo">
        Pančevo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sombor" title="Sombor">
        Sombor
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sremska_Mitrovica" title="Sremska Mitrovica">
        Sremska Mitrovica
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Vr%C5%A1ac" title="Vršac">
        Vršac
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">

      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographic_history_of_Vojvodina" title="Demographic history of Vojvodina">
        Demographic history of Vojvodina
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Vojvodina" title="Ethnic groups of Vojvodina">
        Ethnic groups of Vojvodina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Vojvodina" title="Religion in Vojvodina">
        Religion in Vojvodina
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Vojvodina" title="Languages of Vojvodina">
        Languages of Vojvodina
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Vojvodina is more diverse than the rest of Serbia with more than 25 ethnic groups and six languages which are in the official use by the provincial administration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
