       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iriski_venac.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1371" data-file-width="944" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iriski_venac.jpg/170px-Iriski_venac.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iriski_venac.jpg/255px-Iriski_venac.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Iriski_venac.jpg/340px-Iriski_venac.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iriski_venac.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Iri%C5%A1ki_Venac_Tower" title="Iriški Venac Tower">
          Iriški Venac Tower
         </a>
         , Fruška Gora
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There are two daily newspapers published in Vojvodina,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dnevnik_(Serbia)" title="Dnevnik (Serbia)">
         Dnevnik
        </a>
       </i>
       in Serbian and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Magyar_Sz%C3%B3" title="Magyar Szó">
         Magyar Szó
        </a>
       </i>
       in Hungarian. Monthly and weekly publications in minority languages include
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hrvatska_rije%C4%8D" title="Hrvatska riječ">
         Hrvatska riječ
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Croatian Word") in Croatian,
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Hlas_%C4%BDudu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Hlas Ľudu (page does not exist)">
         Hlas Ľudu
        </a>
       </i>
       ("The Voice of the People") in Slovak,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertatea_(Vojvodina)" title="Libertatea (Vojvodina)">
         Libertatea
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Freedom") in Romanian, and
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ruske_slovo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ruske slovo (page does not exist)">
         Руске слово
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Rusyn Word") in Rusyn. There is also
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bunjeva%C4%8Dke_novine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bunjevačke novine (page does not exist)">
         Bunjevačke novine
        </a>
       </i>
       ("The Bunjevac newspaper") in Bunjevac.
      </p>
      <p>
       Public Broadcasting Service of Vojvodina was founded in 1974 as Radio Television of Novi Sad, as an equal member of the association of JRT – Yugoslav Radio Television. Radio Novi Sad's first broadcast was on November 29, 1949. During the NATO bombing in the spring of 1999, the RT Novi Sad building of 20 thousand square meters was completely destroyed along with its basic production and technical premises . The Venac terrestrial broadcasting site was heavily damaged.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Radio-Television of Vojvodina produces and broadcasts regional programming on two channels, RTV1 (Serbian language) and RTV2 (minority languages), and three radio frequencies: Radio Novi Sad 1 (Serbian), Radio Novi Sad 2 (Hungarian), Radio Novi Sad 3 (other minority communities).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2810" data-file-width="5184" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG/220px-Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG/330px-Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG/440px-Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Serbia_Vojka_from_southwest_IMG_9207.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Vojvodina is known as Serbia's breadbasket
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The economy of Vojvodina is largely based on developed food industry and fertile agricultural soil. Agriculture is a priority sector in Vojvodina. Traditionally, it has always been a significant part of the local economy and a generator of positive results, due to the abundance of fertile agricultural land which makes up 84% of its territory. The share of agribusiness in the total industrial production is 40%, that is 30% in the total exports of Vojvodina. Metal industry of Vojvodina has a long tradition and consists of smaller metal processing companies for components manufacturing and, to a lesser extent, of original equipment manufacturers (OEM) with their own brand name products. Vojvodina Metal Cluster gathers 116 companies with 6,300 employees. Other branches of industry are also developed such as the chemical industry, electrical industry, oil industry and construction industry. In the past decade, ICT sector has been growing rapidly and has taken significant role in Vojvodina's economic development.
      </p>
      <p>
       High- tech sector is a fast-growing sector in Vojvodina. Software development represents the main source of revenue, particularly development of ERP solutions, Java applications and mobile applications. IT sector companies mainly deal with software outsourcing, based on demands of international clients or with development of their own software products for purposes of domestic and international market. Vojvodina pays particular attention to interregional and cross-border economic cooperation, as well as to implementation of priorities defined within the EU Strategy for the Danube Region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vojvodina.gov.rs_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-vojvodina.gov.rs-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the companies from Vojvodina:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Naftna_Industrija_Srbije" title="Naftna Industrija Srbije">
         Naftna Industrija Srbije
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Srbijagas" title="Srbijagas">
         Srbijagas
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HIP_Petrohemija" title="HIP Petrohemija">
         HIP Petrohemija
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Apatin_Brewery" title="Apatin Brewery">
         Apatin Brewery
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Novi_Sad_Fair" title="Novi Sad Fair">
         Novosadski sajam
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Vojvodina promotes its investment potentials through the
       <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina_Investment_Promotion" title="Vojvodina Investment Promotion">
        Vojvodina Investment Promotion
       </a>
       (VIP) agency, which was founded by the Parliament of the Autonomous Province of Vojvodina.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       There are many important roads which pass through Vojvodina. First of all, the motorway
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A1_(Serbia)" title="A1 (Serbia)">
        A1 motorway
       </a>
       which goes from Central Europe and the Horgos border crossing to Hungary, via Novi Sad to Belgrade and further to the southeast toward Niš, where it branches: one way leads east to the border with Bulgaria; the other to the south, towards Greece. Motorway
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A3_(Serbia)" title="A3 (Serbia)">
        A3
       </a>
       in Srem separates the west, towards the neighboring Croatia and further to Western Europe. Besides, there is a network of regional and local roads and railway lines. The three largest rivers in Vojvodina are navigable stream. Danube River with a length of 588 kilometers and its tributaries Tisa (168 km), Sava (206 km) and Bega (75 km). Among them was dug extensive network of irrigation canals, drainage and transport, with a total length of 939 km, of which 673 km navigable.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Vojvodina&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Vojvodina" title="Tourism in Vojvodina">
        Tourism in Vojvodina
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Tourist destinations in Vojvodina include well known
       <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">
        Orthodox
       </a>
       monasteries on
       <a href="/wiki/Fru%C5%A1ka_Gora" title="Fruška Gora">
        Fruška Gora
       </a>
       mountain, numerous hunting grounds, cultural-historical monuments, different folklores, interesting galleries and museums, plain landscapes with a lot of greenery, big rivers, canals and lakes, sandy terrain
       <a href="/wiki/Deliblatska_Pe%C5%A1%C4%8Dara" title="Deliblatska Peščara">
        Deliblatska Peščara
       </a>
       ("the European Sahara"), etc. In the last few years,
       <a href="/wiki/Exit_(festival)" title="Exit (festival)">
        Exit
       </a>
       has been very popular among the European summer music festivals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

                       </a>

                  <tr>
                   <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
                    <div>
                     <ul>
                      <li>
                       <sup>
                        <small>
                         1
                        </small>
                       </sup>
                       <span class="wrap">
                        <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">
                         Kosovo
                        </a>
                        is the subject of a territorial dispute between the
                        <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">
                         Republic of Kosovo
                        </a>
                        and the
                        <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
                         Republic of Serbia
                        </a>
                        . The Republic of Kosovo
                        <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">
                         unilaterally declared independence
                        </a>
                        on 17 February 2008, but
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia%27s_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="Serbia's reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">
                         Serbia continues to claim
                        </a>
                        it as part of its
                        <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">
                         own sovereign territory
                        </a>
                        . The two governments
                        <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">
                         began to normalise relations
                        </a>
                        in 2013, as part of the
                        <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">
                         Brussels Agreement
                        </a>
                        . Kosovo has received formal recognition as an independent state from
                        <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">
                         111
                        </a>
                        out of 193
                        <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
                         United Nations
                        </a>
                        <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">
                         member states
                        </a>
                        .
                       </span>
                      </li>
                     </ul>
                    </div>
                   </td>
                  </tr>
                 </table>
                </div>

                     <tr>
                      <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3">
                       <div>
                        <sup>
                         <small>
                          1
                         </small>
                        </sup>
                        <span class="wrap">
                         <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">
                          Kosovo
                         </a>
                         is the subject of a territorial dispute between the
                         <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">
                          Republic of Kosovo
                         </a>
                         and the
                         <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
                          Republic of Serbia
                         </a>
                         . The Republic of Kosovo
                         <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">
                          unilaterally declared independence
                         </a>
                         on 17 February 2008, but
                         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbia%27s_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="Serbia's reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">
                          Serbia continues to claim
                         </a>
                         it as part of its
                         <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Province_of_Kosovo_and_Metohija" title="Autonomous Province of Kosovo and Metohija">
                          own sovereign territory
                         </a>
                         . The two governments
                         <a href="/wiki/Belgrade%E2%80%93Pristina_negotiations" title="Belgrade–Pristina negotiations">
                          began to normalise relations
                         </a>
                         in 2013, as part of the
                         <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Agreement_(2013)" title="Brussels Agreement (2013)">
                          Brussels Agreement
                         </a>
                         . Kosovo has received formal recognition as an independent state from
                         <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Kosovo" title="International recognition of Kosovo">
                          111
                         </a>
                         out of 193
                         <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
                          United Nations
                         </a>
                         <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">
                          member states
                         </a>
                         .
                        </span>
                       </div>
                      </td>
                     </tr>
                    </table>
                   </td>
                  </tr>
                 </table>
                </div>
               </div>
              </td>
             </tr>
            </table>
